  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

<div id="review_1494996997" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1494996997" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1494996997?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780020442400" href="/book/show/317501.Prince_Caspian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=books-i-read-growing-up">books-i-read-growing-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/922495-patrick?shelf=best-books-for-kids">best-books-for-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1494996997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10813663503473906642">I read this aloud to my older boy, age 6.<br/><br/>It's a good book, and he enjoyed it, but didn't ring the bell in the same way Lion, Witch and the Wardrobe did. I think the biggest reason for this, was that it wasn't as accessible to him.<br/><br/>The first issue was the non-linear story. Which has the potential to confuse. Later, Lewis splits the party in a way that divides the action in the story.<br/><br/>But the biggest issue is that the characters lapse into archaic, courtly English when the a bunch of the people are </span>
  <span id="freeText10813663503473906642" style="display:none">I read this aloud to my older boy, age 6.<br /><br />It's a good book, and he enjoyed it, but didn't ring the bell in the same way Lion, Witch and the Wardrobe did. I think the biggest reason for this, was that it wasn't as accessible to him.<br /><br />The first issue was the non-linear story. Which has the potential to confuse. Later, Lewis splits the party in a way that divides the action in the story.<br /><br />But the biggest issue is that the characters lapse into archaic, courtly English when the a bunch of the people are talking at the end of the book. (Because the siblings used to be kings and queens, and they're talking with the nobility of the Telemarines.) <br /><br />It's not just unfamiliar language to children. It's unfamiliar and archaic language. (Doubly archaic now, as Lewis wrote these 50 years ago.) My boy couldn't follow it at all, as there were 2-4 unfamiliar terms used in every sentence, and context can only stretch so far.) Because of that, Oot couldn't understand whole sections of the climax of the book, when the Telmarines were talking among themselves, and planning on betraying their king. (A vital plot point he couldn't get because it was only made explicit in this dialogue.) <br /><br />As a result, I had to skim, skip, or summarize big chunks of the book so he could get it. Maybe in a year or two, he would have been fine. (Also, keep in mind that my boy is extremely vocabulary. We've been reading to him since he was six months old. Results with your own child may vary.) <br /><br />Sexism a little more present here, but not oppressive or malicious. Still, you can't deny that the boys go off to duel and do battle stuff, while the girls hang out with Aslan and go wake the trees. <br /><br />This book had better characters that the first book of the series. Nikabrik is a great example of a good guy gone bad. Trumpkin and Trufflehunter are great as well. <br /><br />But Reepicheep is the real star here. Perhaps the best character in all of Narnia, excepting Aslan himself. <br /><br />Lastly, and mostly as a side note, Lewis really knocked it out of the park in terms of names. Nikabrik is a great name for a venomous black dwarf. Glenstorm the proud centaur. Wimbleweather the dim but kind giant. <br /><br />And Reepicheep, of course. I don't know if a name has ever fit a character better than "Reepicheep" does....</span>
  <a data-text-id="10813663503473906642" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2177559656" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2177559656" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2177559656?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2177559656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11431483125843494426"><blockquote>
  <i>You doubt your value. Don't run from who you are.</i>
</blockquote> The Pevensie siblings (Peter, Susan, Edmund and Lucy) spent the last year daydreaming about Narnia. Despite the horrors of the White Witch, but they constantly think about <b>returning to Narnia</b> for they are only truly themselves when they are with Aslan. <blockquote>
  <i>Feeling like the voice she liked best in all the world was calling her name.</i>
</blockquote>And when they suddenly find themselves <b>thrust back into Narnia, </b>they discover one very, very important thing: <blockquote>
  </blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText11431483125843494426" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>You doubt your value. Don't run from who you are.</i>
</blockquote> The Pevensie siblings (Peter, Susan, Edmund and Lucy) spent the last year daydreaming about Narnia. Despite the horrors of the White Witch, but they constantly think about <b>returning to Narnia</b> for they are only truly themselves when they are with Aslan. <blockquote>
  <i>Feeling like the voice she liked best in all the world was calling her name.</i>
</blockquote>And when they suddenly find themselves <b>thrust back into Narnia, </b>they discover one very, very important thing: <blockquote>
  <i>Things never happen the same way twice.</i>
</blockquote> The siblings soon realize that<b> time moves far differently</b> in Narnia than it does in the real world. A thousand years have passed and everyone they once knew have long since passed. It's up to them to put the one, true prince on Narnia's throne and<b> right the world </b>that has gone so far astray.<br /><br />I did appreciate how C. S. Lewis wrote his female characters with a bit of spunk and sass in them:<blockquote>
  <i>“That's the worst of girls," said Edmund to Peter and the Dwarf. "They never can carry a map in their heads."<br />"That's because our heads have something inside them," said Lucy.</i>
</blockquote> Though, I did notice that the gals never got to do any sword-fighting and did spend a lot of time being protected by their brothers. Ah well.<b> It was a sign of the times.</b><br /><br />And while I really enjoyed catching up with Lucy and co.,<b> I was hugely disappointed </b>to learn about the time-jump. I just couldn't believe that C. S. Lewis wrote off the Beaver family and Mr. Tumnus so quickly. We still have Aslan but <b>I missed the side-characters I fell in love with.</b><br /><br /><b>Audiobook Comments</b><br />Read by Lynn Redgrave and it was rather well done. Enjoyable to listen to!<br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>

          </span>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/614778-ahmad-sharabiani?shelf=childrens-young-readers">childrens-young-readers</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer75981267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14514360642315441829">Prince Caspian: the return to Narnia (Chronicles of Narnia, #2), C.S. Lewis<br/><br/>Prince Caspian (originally published as Prince Caspian: The Return to Narnia) is a high fantasy novel for children by C. S. Lewis, published by Geoffrey Bles in 1951. It was the second published of seven novels in The Chronicles of Narnia (1950–1956), and Lewis had finished writing it in 1949, before the first book was out. It is volume four in recent editions of the series, sequenced according to Narnia history. Like the</span>
  <span id="freeText14514360642315441829" style="display:none">Prince Caspian: the return to Narnia (Chronicles of Narnia, #2), C.S. Lewis<br /><br />Prince Caspian (originally published as Prince Caspian: The Return to Narnia) is a high fantasy novel for children by C. S. Lewis, published by Geoffrey Bles in 1951. It was the second published of seven novels in The Chronicles of Narnia (1950–1956), and Lewis had finished writing it in 1949, before the first book was out. It is volume four in recent editions of the series, sequenced according to Narnia history. Like the others, it was illustrated by Pauline Baynes and her work has been retained in many later editions. <br /><br />Prince Caspian features "return to Narnia" by the four Pevensie children of the first novel, about a year later in England but 1300 years later in Narnia. It is the only book of The Chronicles with men dominating Narnia. The talking animals and mythical beings are oppressed, and some may be endangered. The English siblings are legendary Kings and Queens of Narnia and are magically recalled once again as children by the refugee Prince Caspian.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 2002 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: ماجراهای نارنیا - کتاب دوم: شاهزاده کاسپین؛ نویسنده: کلاویو استیپلز لوئیس (از سال 1898 میلادی تا سال 1963 میلادی ) مترجم: امید اقتداری؛ منوچهر کریم زاده؛ تهران، 1379؛ در 208ص؛ شابک: 9647100043؛ چاپ سوم 1384؛ هفت جلد در 1368 صفحه؛ موضوع داستانهای خیال انگیز برای نوجوانان از نویسندگان انگلیسی - سده 20م<br /><br />مترجم: پیمان اسماعیلیان خامنه؛ تهران، قدیانی، 1386؛ در 284ص؛ شابک 9644178521؛ <br /><br />مترجم: مهناز داوودی؛ تهران، پنجره، 1387؛ در 200ص؛ شابک 9789648890877؛<br /><br />نقل از متن: خرسهای شکم گنده، خیلی مشتاق بودند که، اول ضیافت برگزار شود، و گردهمایی بماند برای بعد؛ شاید برای فردا؛ ص 79؛ سطر 17کتاب<br /><br />ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="14514360642315441829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1286516623?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P " class="user" itemprop="url" name="P " href="/user/show/25327841-p">P </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7806796-prince-caspian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25327841-p?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1286516623" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3276451761832885085"><b>
  <blockquote>“Things never happen the same way twice.” </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487952896i/22067971._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Admittedly Prince Caspian was boring at first for I didn't like the symbolic meaning of the whole book. It was hard to read and that incredible ending nearly shut me out from enjoying, it's abrupt and unsatisfied at all. Although I quie liked the movie, the book is so much different. The pace is excruciatingly slow. I didn't like the over-descriptive narration talking about everything including flowers, sky, and trees.<br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>“Wouldn't it be dreadful if s</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText3276451761832885085" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>“Things never happen the same way twice.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487952896i/22067971._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Admittedly Prince Caspian was boring at first for I didn't like the symbolic meaning of the whole book. It was hard to read and that incredible ending nearly shut me out from enjoying, it's abrupt and unsatisfied at all. Although I quie liked the movie, the book is so much different. The pace is excruciatingly slow. I didn't like the over-descriptive narration talking about everything including flowers, sky, and trees.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Wouldn't it be dreadful if some day in our own world, at home, men start going wild inside, like the animals here, and still look like men, so that you'd never know which were which.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487952896ra/22067972.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The first part of this book was acceptable, especially when Peter, Susan, Edmund, and Lucy comes back to Narnia, the vibes of the book is nearly the same as the previous one. But around the middle, the story was a downfall, there're so many subtle meanings between the pages, it gave me such a headache that I had to think about it many times.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487952896ra/22067973.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487952896ra/22067974.gif" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, this book isn't awful. It has the enjoyable parts to keep my attention until the last page. Prince Caspian is as intriguing as always, so much alike his character in the movie.<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>“Feeling like the voice she liked best in all the world was calling her name.” </blockquote>
</b><br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://goo.gl/2jOuq2">https://goo.gl/2jOuq2</a></span>

<div id="review_3497903305" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3497903305" />
    <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is"><img alt="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1516737798p2/4467515.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3497903305?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jasmine from How Useful It Is" href="/user/show/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is">Jasmine from How Useful It Is</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4467515-jasmine-from-how-useful-it-is?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3497903305" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11329418349375765587">This book was an excellent read! I just loved how the story pulled me in. It helped that the characters were well liked and their adventures were exciting. I like Prince Caspian and his curiosities. The stories about the animals were fantastic. It boggled my mind that the time difference between Narnia and real life was so vast! It's also interesting that different people came and took over in the centuries that passed.<br/><br/> The story continued where The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe left off. It</span>
  <span id="freeText11329418349375765587" style="display:none">This book was an excellent read! I just loved how the story pulled me in. It helped that the characters were well liked and their adventures were exciting. I like Prince Caspian and his curiosities. The stories about the animals were fantastic. It boggled my mind that the time difference between Narnia and real life was so vast! It's also interesting that different people came and took over in the centuries that passed.<br /><br /> The story continued where The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe left off. It's a year later and they are at the train station heading back to boarding school. When one moment they felt something pulled them and the next they found themselves in the woods and on an island. They went swimming for awhile and then they explored looking for fresh water to drink. As they explored, they found an apple orchard and an old broken down castle. Peter solved the mystery of the castle and it surprised them all. Somewhere in Narnia a Prince needed help and it explained why the children were brought back to Narnia. The author again narrated the story.<br /><br /> Prince Caspian was well written and a fast paced read! I enjoyed the siblings' relationship. It's also clear there were different personalities in this story. I like the ending because there was mentioned of a portal. I love portals to a parallel universe! That's too bad the siblings didn't stay as long this time as they did their first trip to Narnia. It's cool that their memory was still intact of all their adventures. I enjoyed the humor in this book. I recommend this classic to everyone.<br /><br />xoxo, Jasmine at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com">www.howusefulitis.wordpress.com</a> for more details </span>
  <a data-text-id="11329418349375765587" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=read-with-kids">read-with-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=2020">2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16254355-matthew?shelf=at-home-reading">at-home-reading</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer872556656" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8804922556391663770">Evening reading time with the kids continued with Prince Caspian. Last year we read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2772945145' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe</a> and then we watched both the old cartoon and the recent live action version. The kids frequently asked for the next one, so it was time. Now, I know there is some debate as to the order of the books in The Chronicles of Narnia, but we choose to go with these two first as it seemed like the most cohesive storyline to keep the kid’s attention. <br/><br/>We all enjoyed family time together</span>
  <span id="freeText8804922556391663770" style="display:none">Evening reading time with the kids continued with Prince Caspian. Last year we read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2772945145" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe</a> and then we watched both the old cartoon and the recent live action version. The kids frequently asked for the next one, so it was time. Now, I know there is some debate as to the order of the books in The Chronicles of Narnia, but we choose to go with these two first as it seemed like the most cohesive storyline to keep the kid’s attention. <br /><br />We all enjoyed family time together with this book, which was a reread for me. We had to break the chapters up because they were kind of long to hold the attention of a 6 and 8-year-old. Also, the language is a bit complex at times and I found myself getting all turned around while reading it out loud. Several times we had to stop and go back over a section to make sure we all understood what just happened (not just the kids!) Also, Lewis loves his run on, comma-delineated sentences!<br /><br />This is a great series for some classic fantasy. It is especially nice if you don’t want to commit to some of the larger classic fantasy tomes. And, while they don’t stick exactly to the plot, a few of the Chronicles have movies to watch afterwards – which is always a bonus for the kids! However, the Prince Caspian movie is over two and a half hours long, so we had to take it in chunks.<br /><br />Next stop – The Voyage of the Dawn Treader!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8804922556391663770" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9075471518132909991"><i>“Lucy buried her head in his mane to hide from his face. But there must have been some magic in his mane. She could feel lion-strength going into her. Quite suddenly she sat up. "I'm sorry, Aslan," she said. "I'm ready now."<br/>"Now you are a lioness," said Aslan. "And now all Narnia will be renewed.”</i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492500736ra/22522218.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><i>*note: a review of this whole series is up on my channel!<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OYsclHHG_Fs'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OYscl...</a></i><br/><br/>It's not easy to review a book so treasured by many readers who have it as a childhood memory, when you </span>

She could feel lion-strength going into her. Quite suddenly she sat up. "I'm sorry, Aslan," she said. "I'm ready now."<br>"Now you are a lioness," said Aslan. "And now all Narnia will be renewed.”</i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492500736ra/22522218.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><i>*note: a review of this whole series is up on my channel!<br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OYsclHHG_Fs">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=OYscl...</a></i><br><br>It's not easy to review a book so treasured by many readers who have it as a childhood memory, when you read it for the first time as an adult, with the mind and the heart of a grown-up. I started reading this series in publication order, knowing only the main plot of the first one (because, <i>alas</i> of having seen the movie first), and I was very curious of knowing the rest of the story. Unfortunately, I cannot feel the same love and attachment to these characters as I do, for example, to Harry Potter; but I still like them all, especially Susan. And Aslan, of course. <br><br>The plot of this volume was not extremely interesting for me, I guess I find these books to be a little too short for a fantasy book - I like to have a more immersive experience when I read this genre - even though I understand very much that is because of the target age. I liked very much the character of Caspian, and his story was my favourite part of the book. And of course, the whole metaphor of the coming of Aslan, very moving. Anyway, I surely will go on with the series, but maybe not right now. I am still curious to know what happens in the other books!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551905215ra/27165096.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2219833354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer185063561220753387">One year has passed since Peter, Susan, Edmund, and Lucy went to Narnia through an old Wardrobe and met the bad white witch and the righteous lion. Now they are sitting on a seat at a railway station with trunks and playboxes piled up round them on their way to school. <br/><br/>But Narnia needs them back. <br/>More precisely PRINCE CASPIAN, the true king of Narnia needs them back. <br/><br/>And the children are ready for a new adventure in the land that thousand - years ago they used to be Kings and Queens themselves. </span>
  <span id="freeText185063561220753387" style="display:none">One year has passed since Peter, Susan, Edmund, and Lucy went to Narnia through an old Wardrobe and met the bad white witch and the righteous lion. Now they are sitting on a seat at a railway station with trunks and playboxes piled up round them on their way to school. <br /><br />But Narnia needs them back. <br />More precisely PRINCE CASPIAN, the true king of Narnia needs them back. <br /><br />And the children are ready for a new adventure in the land that thousand - years ago they used to be Kings and Queens themselves. <br /><br />Because time passes at different speeds in Narnia.<br /><br />And now the landscape has changed and the men are ruling the fairytale land. The talking animals and the mythical creatures are hiding trying to survive. Everyone remembers Narnia's golden age and everyone is hoping that a just King will appear and will bring prosperity and safety again to the rightful population of Narnia.<br /><br />There two stories in this book that mingle: The story of the prince Caspian and how he claims this throne and the story of the four children’s return to Narnia. It may look confusing when you read it, but everything will make sense after a certain point in the book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>Then begin a new paragraph…..</i>
</b><br /><br />Sometimes The Chronicles of Narnia remind me the Neverending Story.<br /></span>

<div id="review_1498038135" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1498038135" />
    <a title="Dannii Elle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle"><img alt="Dannii Elle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1508499419p2/44487975.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1498038135?book_show_action=true">Jan 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dannii Elle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dannii Elle" href="/user/show/44487975-dannii-elle">Dannii Elle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title=" 9780001831780" href="/book/show/1045076.Prince_Caspian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=adventurous-acuity">adventurous-acuity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44487975-dannii-elle?shelf=fantastic-fabrications">fantastic-fabrications</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1498038135" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5941217539034682823">This is my fourth journey into the fantastical lands of Narnia, as I have chosen to read the series in chronological rather than publication order.<br/><br/>From the very first line I knew I was sure to love this book as it details the return of the Pevensie children from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch__and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___1_' title='The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #1) by C.S. Lewis' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</a>, the most famous and my most beloved Narnia tale. Only one year later in the human world, and centuries later in Narnian time, the children return to find their beloved castle an ivy-clad ruin and th</span>
  <span id="freeText5941217539034682823" style="display:none">This is my fourth journey into the fantastical lands of Narnia, as I have chosen to read the series in chronological rather than publication order.<br /><br />From the very first line I knew I was sure to love this book as it details the return of the Pevensie children from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/100915.The_Lion__the_Witch__and_the_Wardrobe__Chronicles_of_Narnia___1_" title="The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe (Chronicles of Narnia, #1) by C.S. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</a>, the most famous and my most beloved Narnia tale. Only one year later in the human world, and centuries later in Narnian time, the children return to find their beloved castle an ivy-clad ruin and the land they knew and loved altered beyond all recognition. Another form of evil has taken control of the lands and the children must once again work with the magical Narnian beasts to free it from the tyrant's control.<br /><br />Whilst I adored the actual story, some elements of it did make me wince a little. Referring to some little girls as 'plump' and mentioning their 'fat legs' seemed like an unnecessary addition to the text but I also need to remember that these books weren't penned in this century, where such writing is unacceptable.<br /><br />This entire series touches me on such a deep emotional level, despite the simplicity of the tales. It is such a wonderful feeling to read something that ends with such purity and goodness. I think this is the magic of reading stories aimed at children: in the adult genre this suspended belief would not be tolerated and the 'happily ever afters' would not be believed. We often look for more complex conclusions, but it is so refreshing to read something where good is sure to conquer evil and be content that all that is wrong will be rightfully restored.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5941217539034682823" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_38136934" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38136934" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/645979-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495382717p2/645979.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38136934?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/645979-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780020442400" href="/book/show/317501.Prince_Caspian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/645979-amanda?shelf=fer-teenagers-kids-and-younguns">fer-teenagers-kids-and-younguns</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/645979-amanda?shelf=2008">2008</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/645979-amanda?shelf=fantasy-and-some-sci-fi">fantasy-and-some-sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38136934" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9479286537289916785">November 19, 2008. I've read these books a zillion and one times and surely I shall read them a zillion more. Because every single time, I realize new truths and find more honor in their pages. <br/><br/>Today, I've read a passage that I find disturbing and quite out of character for CS Lewis: <br/><br/>p.72<i> "Shall we go farther up for you, up to the crags? There's an Ogre or two and a Hag that we could introduce you to, up there." "Certainly not," said Caspian. "I should think not, indeed," said Trufflehunter. "We</i></span>
  <span id="freeText9479286537289916785" style="display:none">November 19, 2008. I've read these books a zillion and one times and surely I shall read them a zillion more. Because every single time, I realize new truths and find more honor in their pages. <br /><br />Today, I've read a passage that I find disturbing and quite out of character for CS Lewis: <br /><br />p.72<i> "Shall we go farther up for you, up to the crags? There's an Ogre or two and a Hag that we could introduce you to, up there." "Certainly not," said Caspian. "I should think not, indeed," said Trufflehunter. "We want none of that sort on our side."</i><br /><br />Seems a bit racist, if you ask me. It really makes me wonder exactly what CS Lewis is getting at here. It's totally the opposite of what happens in <i>The Last Battle</i> when Aslan sorts the good guys from the bad guys by whether they're good oir evil in their hearts. So anyway, it seems weird and I don't like it. The Hag does ends up being a bad guy in the end, but still... I dunno. <br /><br />I'll keep reading and blame the racism on the 1950s for now. <br /><br />Oh yeah, as a side note, whenever I read British literature, I talk to myself in a British accent and rhythm for a while afterward. It's so dorky!!!<br /><br />Later...<br />I've read a bit more now. The race issue didn't come up again. <br /><br />The battle scenes are not the same as you might see these days. There's something more frank and quick about them. Lewis doesn't explain every little move and maneuver, so in fact, if you're reading too fast, you might even miss a fight going on. Here's an example of a battle overview without much in the way of specifics:<br />P. 187<br /><i>But the new bout went well. Peter now seemed to be able to make some use of his shield, and he certainly made good use of his feet. He was almost playing Tig with Miraz now, keeping out of range shifting his ground, making the enemy work.</i><br /><br />I think if this book had been written today by a different author, it might be about 500 pages of battle scenes. I'm glad its not. Instead, the book is more about people standing on the side of good. Here's a passage that I just love which describes Edmund who may be a boy, but is also a king:<br />P.174<i>An hour later two great lords in the army of Miraz, the Lord Glozelle and the Lord Sopespian, strolling along their lines and picking their teeth after breakfast, looked up and saw coming down to them from the wood the Centaur and Giant Wembleweather, whom they had seen before in battle, and between them a figure they could not recognise. Nor indeed would the other boys at Edmund's school have recognised him if they could have seen him at that moment. For Aslan had breathed on him at their meeting and a kind of greatness hung about him. </i><br /><br />Ahhhhh... See? For Narnia and the North!<br /><br /><br />Also, you Tolkien fans will recognize the onslaught of trees which comes in at the end of the battle--Two Towers--and the river emerging (with the help of Bacchus and his grapevines) to take out the bridge and thwart the enemy in its path--Fellowship. Who came up with it first, I wonder... :)<br /><br /><br /><br />Later still...<br />As I finish reading this lovely little novel, allow me to <i>drop off to sleep with feet towards the fire and good friends on either side...</i> Thank you, Mr. Lewis. I <i> have</i> had a time. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9479286537289916785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3354007968" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3354007968" />
    <a title="Shruti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30505436-shruti"><img alt="Shruti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602233159p2/30505436.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3354007968?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shruti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shruti" href="/user/show/30505436-shruti">Shruti</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30505436-shruti?shelf=fantasy-series">fantasy-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3354007968" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10953783118420430735">The second book in The Chronicles of Narnia, Prince Caspian does not disappoint. The story has a slow start and isn't as gripping as The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe, but I was just glad to read a new Pevensie siblings adventure. <br/><br/>A number of new characters were introduced, each having incredibly peculiar names that I loved but find hard to recollect now. Half the story focussed on Prince Caspian and how Narnia transformed from being a land of free, talking, magical creatures to a land of stu</span>
  <span id="freeText10953783118420430735" style="display:none">The second book in The Chronicles of Narnia, Prince Caspian does not disappoint. The story has a slow start and isn't as gripping as The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe, but I was just glad to read a new Pevensie siblings adventure. <br /><br />A number of new characters were introduced, each having incredibly peculiar names that I loved but find hard to recollect now. Half the story focussed on Prince Caspian and how Narnia transformed from being a land of free, talking, magical creatures to a land of stubborn men who refused to believe in the existence of said creatures, while the other half dealt with Peter, Susan, Edmund and Lucy's quest to lend help to Prince Caspian. <br /><br />Some plot points did annoy me a bit—one of them being that the boys were sent to make battle plans and do the important stuff while the girls pranced around with Aslan. Given how old this book is and the fact that apart from this, Lewis has never hinted at the girls in the story being any less capable than the boys, I chose to not let this affect how I rated this book. <br /><br />And now, on to the next one!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10953783118420430735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2539422450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2539422450" />
    <a title="Piyangie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie"><img alt="Piyangie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590579939p2/48056505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2539422450?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Piyangie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Piyangie" href="/user/show/48056505-piyangie">Piyangie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780060764920" href="/book/show/782806.Prince_Caspian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=fantasy-classic">fantasy-classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=brittish-lit">brittish-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48056505-piyangie?shelf=my-library">my-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2539422450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7911404612625846233">This book in the chronicles takes us back to a "new" Narnia where the tyrant Miraz is reining. The old Narnia is disappeared and with it the talking beasts, dwarfs, centaurs, dryads and naiads. It is the time for a new and true king for Narnia. To secure this end, the Pevensie children return to Narnia. And with the power, aid and guidance of Alsan, Narnia is rescued from the clutches of Miraz and handed back to the true owners and the true king - Caspian. <br/><br/>This is the most beautifully written bo</span>
  <span id="freeText7911404612625846233" style="display:none">This book in the chronicles takes us back to a "new" Narnia where the tyrant Miraz is reining. The old Narnia is disappeared and with it the talking beasts, dwarfs, centaurs, dryads and naiads. It is the time for a new and true king for Narnia. To secure this end, the Pevensie children return to Narnia. And with the power, aid and guidance of Alsan, Narnia is rescued from the clutches of Miraz and handed back to the true owners and the true king - Caspian. <br /><br />This is the most beautifully written book in the chronicles so far. The beautiful and colourful description of "old" Narnia and its inhabitants (talking beasts, dwarfs, centaurs, dryads and naiads) makes the reader yearns to be there, among them in peace and bliss. It is an adventure story like all others in the chronicles, but all the same it is more than an adventure story. It is also story of equality, justice and righteousness. <br /><br />To me, this is where the characters of Peter, Susan, Edmund and Lucy are at their best. They are fully developed and there is a perfect balance in their ideas of right and wrong. The introductory characters of Prince Caspian and Dr. Cornelius were likable and interesting. They represent bravery, courage and determination. And of course if there is no betrayer, then there is something amiss and incomplete in the story. This is why we meet the traitor and conniver, Nikabrik who tries to take advantage of the hostility between Miraz and Caspian to awaken the white witch. I also like the new characters of talking beasts, especially Reepicheep, the mouse.  And of course, as always, Aslan was the most loved character above all. <br /><br />It was really a fascinating read and I enjoyed it immensely. I've read four books in the chronicles now and so far, Prince Caspian and The Lion, the Witch and the Wardrobe are my favourites. I hope the rest of the series too would be engaging and interesting reads.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7911404612625846233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14557071982371913389" style="display:none">I read this several times as a kid. It was never high up in the series for me. <span id="freeTextContainer1935564067011709277">What can you say. Another fantastic adventure in Narnia! And of course,<br/>I cried at the end. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_712544570" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/712544570" />
    <a title="Bookwraiths" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths"><img alt="Bookwraiths" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353765210p2/14716035.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/712544570?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bookwraiths" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bookwraiths" href="/user/show/14716035-bookwraiths">Bookwraiths</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audio 9781561797875" href="/book/show/1154894.Prince_Caspian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=young_adult">young_adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14716035-bookwraiths?shelf=audio-books">audio-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer712544570" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6354371542271222557">Reviewed at <a href='http://bookwraiths.wordpress.com/2013/09/19/prince-caspian-audio-book-good-fun/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bookwraiths Reviews</a><br/><br/><i>Prince Caspian</i> is the second book in <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i>. <br/><br/>C.S. Lewis begins this tale by revisiting the Pevensie children, who have survived WW II and are at a train station waiting to head off to boarding school. While discussing their concerns about being separated, they are suddenly pulled into another world, which they do not immediately recognize as Narnia. Indeed, the land has changed to such an extent that it is only after finding several relics from th</span>
  <span id="freeText6354371542271222557" style="display:none">Reviewed at <a href="http://bookwraiths.wordpress.com/2013/09/19/prince-caspian-audio-book-good-fun/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookwraiths Reviews</a><br /><br /><i>Prince Caspian</i> is the second book in <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i>. <br /><br />C.S. Lewis begins this tale by revisiting the Pevensie children, who have survived WW II and are at a train station waiting to head off to boarding school. While discussing their concerns about being separated, they are suddenly pulled into another world, which they do not immediately recognize as Narnia. Indeed, the land has changed to such an extent that it is only after finding several relics from the past that they even begin to suspect that they are not only in Narnia but actually camped in the ruins of Cair Paravel: their former capital and home, where they reigned as high kings and queens of Narnia. <br /><br />Quickly, the siblings begin to understand that while only a small amount of time has passed in their world, many centuries have rolled by in their former home, which has resulted in the ruination of the castle and a changing of the very land itself. This new state of affairs is soon confirmed for the Pevensie children by one Trumpkin the dwarf, who they rescue from the Telmarines: the overlords of the new Narnia.<br /><br />What transpires after Trumpkin’s rescue is what I call the flashback story. Through Trumpkin, C.S. Lewis basically tells Peter, Edmund, Susan, and Lucy (and by default the reader/listener) all about the new Narnia and our title character, Prince Caspian. We hear about the invasion of the Telmarines, the fading of the old ways, the disappearance of the talking animals of Narnia, and the slow waning of all things magical in Narnia. But we also are told about the rightful heir of this new Narnia, Prince Caspian, who wishes to restore the land to its Golden Age when Peter, Edmund, Susan and Lucy ruled from Cair Paravel and who is even now in hiding with the Old Narnians, trying desperately to restore overthrow his wicked uncle and bring peace, prosperity, and magic back to the land.<br /><br />Only after hearing all this back story, does C.S. Lewis allow our four children to head out into the world on their grand adventure to aid Prince Caspian and thereby restore Narnia to its former glory.<br /><br />I enjoyed this book via audio book (which is a fairly new “reading” medium for me) and found the experience enjoyable and the actors’ performances well done. Specifically, this audio book did a great job of presenting the ambiance of Narnia’s different locals by description as well as sound effects, which on the whole livened up a fairly straightforward tale.<br /><br />As far as the story itself, I found myself conflicted on it: liking some things about it yet disliking others.<br /><br /><i>LIKES</i><br /><br />1) C.S. Lewis did not try to just rewrite <i>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</i>, but gives the reader a whole new Narnia experience. While the old Narnians - fauns, centaurs, talking animals, nymphs, living trees - are still around, they are now in hiding; driven to the edge of extinction by the Telmarines, who have not only conquered the land but turned it into a near non-magical world. This leads to a darker feeling to the story and allows a reader to see Peter, Edmund, Susan and Lucy both overjoyed at being back in Narnia but aghast at its desecration.<br /><br />2) Lewis allows the Pevensie children to actually grow up. Peter and Susan are shown as near adults, who are becoming blind to the magic in Narnia, while Edmund and Lucy rise to the forefront as the keepers of that magic. Especially illustrative of the “growth” of the characters were Lucy’s struggle to rediscover Aslan and Edmund’s stance as her steadfast supporter.<br /><br /><b>DISLIKES</b><br /><br />1) There just isn’t much suspense in this story. The children show up, rescue Trumpkin, get told all about what is going on then head out to join up with Prince Caspian. The majority of the story Peter, Edmund, Susan and Lucy really do not do anything, and even at the climax of the adventure, they are more bystanders than participants. Honestly, all the suspense and actions, which is described in the story, deal with Caspian and are “told” to us in flashback, not experienced as Caspian is living them. While I understand why C.S. Lewis crafted the story this way (The four children are a reader’s link to Narnia) I believe Caspian’s story itself would have been a more rousing tale.<br /><br />2) Things just work out too easily, even for what is obviously intended as a children’s story. For instance, Caspian grows up, becomes enamored with stories of ancient Narnia and up pops a half-dwarf tutor, who can provide all the lore Caspian needs. When he seeks refuge, the mysterious and little seen “old” Narnians turn up and take the Telmarine Prince into their hearts almost immediately. Each of these things seemed a bit rushed to me, but then again, it could be yet another draw back of flashback stories.<br /><br />All in all, this was an enjoyable listening experience, and much better than the movie - at least in my opinion. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6354371542271222557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Erin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Erin" href="/user/show/17957823-erin">Erin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2188009362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4478561432216221507">Book #4 in The Chronicles of Narnia, Prince Caspian reunites readers with Peter, Susan, Edmund, and Lucy who find themselves traveling back to Narnia. But this Narnia is different from the one which they left. In fact, many years have passed and their time in Narnia has become something of a legend that no one quite believes to be true. That also includes the great lion known as Aslan. The quartet soon become entwined with the fate of a young man known as Prince Caspian. Caspian is fleeing from </span>
  <span id="freeText4478561432216221507" style="display:none">Book #4 in The Chronicles of Narnia, Prince Caspian reunites readers with Peter, Susan, Edmund, and Lucy who find themselves traveling back to Narnia. But this Narnia is different from the one which they left. In fact, many years have passed and their time in Narnia has become something of a legend that no one quite believes to be true. That also includes the great lion known as Aslan. The quartet soon become entwined with the fate of a young man known as Prince Caspian. Caspian is fleeing from his uncle, the king, who wants to kill him. Adventure and magic follow and a lot of new characters snuggle their way into reader's hearts. <br /><br />I must confess that when reading The Lion, The Witch, and the Wardrobe as a child, Lucy was always my favorite. With Prince Caspian, I am adding dear Edmund to the list. But goodness Peter and Susan were so condescending to their sister. I took this as a hint from C.S. Lewis that this will be their last Narnian adventure. This book more than makes up for book 3 (The Horse and his boy)which failed to impress me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4478561432216221507" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780060234843" href="/book/show/1040662.Prince_Caspian">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=ya-ya-land">ya-ya-land</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2190064-nenia-socially-awkward-trash-panda-campbell?shelf=you-can-watch-it-on-the-telly">you-can-watch-it-on-the-telly</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2449320123" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13330208006653102264"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>I recently decided to reread the <i>Narnia </i>series, only I decided to go about it in chronological order instead of publication order. What does this change? It means you read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448249462' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE MAGICIAN'S NEPHEW</a> first, instead of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448663278' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE LION, THE WITCH AND THE WARDROBE</a>, that there's a book about totally random characters sandwiched in between TLTW (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448926254' rel='nofollow noopener'>THE HORSE AND HIS BOY</a>) before the series settles back into the usual order.<br/><br/><br/><br/>I never really liked PRINCE CASPIAN </span>
  <span id="freeText13330208006653102264" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>I recently decided to reread the <i>Narnia </i>series, only I decided to go about it in chronological order instead of publication order. What does this change? It means you read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448249462" rel="nofollow noopener">THE MAGICIAN'S NEPHEW</a> first, instead of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448663278" rel="nofollow noopener">THE LION, THE WITCH AND THE WARDROBE</a>, that there's a book about totally random characters sandwiched in between TLTW (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448926254" rel="nofollow noopener">THE HORSE AND HIS BOY</a>) before the series settles back into the usual order.<br><br><br><br>I never really liked PRINCE CASPIAN before. I tried reading it as a teenager and ended up not finishing, and in the BBC series based on these books (which I watched many times), parts of the <i>Prince Caspian </i>TV movie were almost unwatchable because the battle scenes were so <i>tedious</i>. I think that's where this book chiefly differs from the other books, which are more adventure-type stories, whereas this is like a child's version of GoT.<br><br><br><br><br><br>The Pevensie kids are all waiting at a train station to be sent to boarding school when they find themselves sucked back into <i>Narnia</i>. Or, at least, what they think is Narnia, because it's completely different from the Narnia they knew. As it turns out, several hundred years have gone by since they ended up returning home via the Lantern Wastes, and magic has all but been forgotten. They find out from a dwarf that these invaders called "Telmarines" appeared in Narnia one day and assumed rule, and while the current heir is Prince Caspian, his evil uncle has staged a coup to assume regent, and since his wife is pregnant, plans to kill off Caspian, too.<br><br><br><br>All of the talking animals and magic creatures have been forced into hiding, but they are about to come out and stage a civil war. Caspian, who has Susan's magic horn (you know, the one Aslan gave to her instead of a weapon because he sucks), brought her, Peter, Lucy, and Edmund here just in time for the final battle, which ends up being weirdly anticlimactic. Then things get weirder.<br><br><br><br>I didn't really liked the characters in this book that much. It was like all the development they underwent in TLTW had flown out the window. Susan, in particular, is portrayed as a raging you-know-what, whereas Peter is even more condescending, and Lucy even more sulky when she doesn't get her way. Edmund was actually decent here, and I think it's probably because his actions in TLTW ironically made him a much better person, because he's still haunted by his bad choices. Prince Caspian wasn't much better. He was very immature. I liked him much better in the TV movie.<br><br><br><br>Also, does anyone else think it's weird/unfair that at this point, Susan and Peter are told that they can never come back to Narnia because they're too old? What does that mean? The Telmarines were all much older when they came to Narnia, so presumably age is not an issue. Peter drops it so casually, too, and doesn't go into detail or seem much bothered about it at all, when you would think that such a reveal would be utterly devastating. After all, if you consider the end of TLTW canon, Peter actually spent <i>decades </i>living in Narnia, becoming an adult before reverting back to a boy (what), so he really did spend half his life here essentially, only to be kicked out by a holier-than-thou lion.<br><br><br><br>Additionally, I'm super curious about how time works in this series. THE MAGICIAN'S NEPHEW treats us to the genesis of Narnia, and that was about one hundred years before this book (set in Victorian times), and given how time works in Narnia, we can probably assume that was millions of years ago in Narnia times. I think in this book, about a year has passed in between TLTW and PRINCE CASPIAN, which equates to a couple <i>hundred </i>years in Narnia. But then, when the kids find out about the horn, they ask what time it was blown, and the dwarf tells them "Oh, around 9am." And someone - I forget who - says, "Oh, that's the time we were sitting at the train station!" I found that really jarring, because it's been made pretty clear up to that point that time in Narnia doesn't correspond to our world much at all (hence the reason her siblings first thought she was lying when she thought she'd been in Narnia for hours and only a few seconds had gone by). That seems like a pretty egregious mistake. I'm surprised C.S. Lewis's publisher didn't catch that, the first time around.<br><br><br><br>3 to 3.5 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="13330208006653102264" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WL+TVnLCg8eD9eiTfuIs1dgX9YxYrraA0+4ZPwLQf5RimfqEyZxKryTeXPKJFyYKDkgSRJYjOOeIkF+Oz5ONDg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Wx60GW0r7dqcF6PHG2+tTj2xMcUucrihxqOPezQXCSthON3L1nUksjs8F6bsmqeR6+7WDeD/Nsad3cnK+VT7sQ==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer10105770188508694787"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br/><br/><br/>Clive Staples Lewis was one of the intellectual giants of the twentieth century and arguably one of the most influential writers of his day. He was a Fellow and Tutor in English Literature at Oxford University until 1954. He was unanimously elected to the Chair of Medieval and Renaissance Literature at Cambridge</span>
  <span id="freeText10105770188508694787" style="display:none"><i>Librarian Note: There is more than one author in the Goodreads database with this name.</i><br /><br /><br />Clive Staples Lewis was one of the intellectual giants of the twentieth century and arguably one of the most influential writers of his day. He was a Fellow and Tutor in English Literature at Oxford University until 1954. He was unanimously elected to the Chair of Medieval and Renaissance Literature at Cambridge University, a position he held until his retirement. He wrote more than thirty books, allowing him to reach a vast audience, and his works continue to attract thousands of new readers every year. His most distinguished and popular accomplishments include <i>Mere Christianity</i>, <i>Out of the Silent Planet</i>, <i>The Great Divorce</i>, <i>The Screwtape Letters</i>, and the universally acknowledged classics <i>The Chronicles of Narnia</i>. To date, the Narnia books have sold over 100 million copies and been transformed into three major motion pictures.<br /><br />Lewis was married to poet <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/467360.Joy_Davidman" title="Joy Davidman" rel="nofollow noopener">Joy Davidman</a>.<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1988716._W_H__Lewis" title=" W.H. Lewis" rel="nofollow noopener"> W.H. Lewis</a> was his elder brother]</span>
  <a data-text-id="10105770188508694787" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
